  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_25e92e7a-4415-40be-954e-459153dc009c'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer14641982838227157380">Amy and Elder have finally left the oppressive walls of the spaceship<i> Godspeed</i> behind. They're ready to start life afresh--to build a home--on Centauri-Earth, the planet that Amy has traveled 25 trillion miles across the universe to experience.<br/><br/> But this new Earth isn't the paradise Amy had been hoping for.   <span id="freeText14641982838227157380" style="display:none">Amy and Elder have finally left the oppressive walls of the spaceship<i> Godspeed</i> behind. They're ready to start life afresh--to build a home--on Centauri-Earth, the planet that Amy has traveled 25 trillion miles across the universe to experience.<br /><br /> But this new Earth isn't the paradise Amy had been hoping for. There are giant pterodactyl-like birds, purple flowers with mind-numbing toxins, and mysterious, unexplained ruins that hold more secrets than their stone walls first let on. The biggest secret of all? <i>Godspeed</i>'s former passengers aren't alone on this planet. And if they're going to stay, they'll have to fight.<br /><br /> Amy and Elder must race to discover who--or what--else is out there if they are to have any hope of saving their struggling colony and building a future together. They will have to look inward to the very core of what makes them human on this, their most harrowing journey yet. Because if the colony collapses? Then everything they have sacrificed--friends, family, life on Earth--will have been for nothing.<br /><br /> FUELED BY LIES.<br /> RULED BY CHAOS.<br /> ALMOST HOME.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_163817366" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/163817366" />
    <a title="Annabelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1235083-annabelle"><img alt="Annabelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1348368292p2/1235083.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/163817366?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annabelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annabelle" href="/user/show/1235083-annabelle">Annabelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1235083-annabelle?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1235083-annabelle?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1235083-annabelle?shelf=love-triangles">love-triangles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1235083-annabelle?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1235083-annabelle?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1235083-annabelle?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1235083-annabelle?shelf=sci-fi-i-actually-like">sci-fi-i-actually-like</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1235083-annabelle?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer163817366" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4865513457934798007">***FINAL RATING: 3.30 STARS***<br/><br/><b>
  <u>CATCHALL</u>
</b><br/>I love a good sci-fi series, especially the wild ones. It's not often we get to experience an entirely new planet, and it was fun to try that in this novel. It's fast-paced, almost a thriller, but doesn't quite reach this level. Even so, it's a major page turner that kept me up late into the night. This last installment was just as brill as the two books that came before. This review kind of makes it sound like I didn't love this book, but believe me, I </span>
  <span id="freeText4865513457934798007" style="display:none">***FINAL RATING: 3.30 STARS***<br /><br /><b>
  <u>CATCHALL</u>
</b><br />I love a good sci-fi series, especially the wild ones. It's not often we get to experience an entirely new planet, and it was fun to try that in this novel. It's fast-paced, almost a thriller, but doesn't quite reach this level. Even so, it's a major page turner that kept me up late into the night. This last installment was just as brill as the two books that came before. This review kind of makes it sound like I didn't love this book, but believe me, I did.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE HERO</u>
</b><br /><u>ELDER</u><br />Elder is okay, I guess. Not the best character ever. I like him more than Amy, which isn't actually saying much but still. He tries to be a good leader, but he's a teenager and we are not the best leaders. He tends to doubt himself when he needs to step up, but he also has no idea when to let go. He's an all right character, but he could have used some improving. I don't hate him, but I have no more real love for him. I used to like him more.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE HEROINE</u>
</b><br /><u>AMY</u><br />I'm not a huge Amy fan. She irritates the living hell out of me. She has these ideals and she's she freaking stubborn and her way is the right way and that is that. And we're supposed to just take that. Guys, Amy is what, seventeen? I sincerely doubt that she holds all the answers to the universe in her hands and that is not okay. She is always, always portrayed as being right in this book and she just really got on my nerves like nothing else.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE PLOT</u>
</b><br />The number one thing that bothered me about this book: <b>It was so freaking ridiculously liberal</b>.<br /><br />Granted, this is a personal issue. and, speaking frankly, I am a teenager and probably have not settled in permanent political views yet. But I was raised as a conservative, and my parents are conservative, and despite the fact that I am liberal in a few select aspects I am still, at this point in my life, mostly a conservative. So, this did affect me. I was so frustrated by all the things that Amy wanted to do and her ideas to govern the colony. However, those are my personal opinions and this might not bother anyone but me.<br /><br />So, moving on. Shades of Earth is very, very fast-paced, but at other times it kind of drags. The pacing is weirdly off. It's always fast or slow, and kind of frustrating. I couldn't get a grip on it. I loved when it moved quickly. It was always fun to hear my heartbeat speed up, but that only made it all the more annoying when everything slowed down.<br /><br />Love the concept, though, and the originality of it. It was fun to explore a new setting. The previous two books took place on the ship, but this one moves away from that. Instead, there's a new planet. New dangers. Unexpected twists. Some things were way too coincidental and unrealistic, but if I let that go and simply enjoyed this for what it was, I had a lot more fun.<br /><br />All in all, I did love this. It wasn't perfect, but perfection is relative anyway. I truly enjoyed this.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE ROMANCE</u>
</b><br />I am not necessarily a huge fan of Amy and Elder's romance. I don't hate it, but it's so goddamn boring. They have no chemistry whatsoever. It's sweet but it lacks substance. I was much more willing to ship Amy with the creepy Chris, who I really didn't like at all, which says a lot. Still, if they want to live a passion-less life together I suppose that's their choice. It felt a lot like a first love thing and just didn't have that extra oomph.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE WRITING</u>
</b><br />Beth has gorgeous writing when it comes to description. She describe Centauri-Earth so vividly that it's almost like we're actually there. There's an incredible level of sensory detail. However, I am not a fan of Amy's and Elder's voice. They just come off to me as so immature and irritating. They've improved since the beginning, but they still needed work. They also aren't nearly distinct enough. I understand the dual-POV thing, but if you're going to do that you need to have distinct, separate voices.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE ENDING</u>
</b><br />I really think that Shades of Earth reached a wonderful ending. It was far from clean, but it was realistic. There's death and destruction and everything isn't neat. There's going to still be changes that have to be made, and they're going to have to rebuild their lives. But it's not a cliffhanger as much as it simply is an open ending. There's more to come, but for us, the story is over. At least for now. However, I wouldn't object to a novella set in this world in the future.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>WRAPUP</u>
</b><br />Not that the Across the Universe series has come to an end, I absolutely cannot wait to see what Beth spins for us next. I'm sure it'll be full of sparkles and romance, and I'm definitely excited. Whether she moves away from sci-fi or stays within the genre, I have high hopes that I'll love it. For old fans of this series, you need to pick this book up ASAP. If you're new to this series, I highly recommend it even if you're queasy about the sic-fi stuff. It's that good.<br /><br />FINE.<br /><br />Find more of my reviews on <a href="http://sparkles-and-lightning.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Sparkles and Lightning</a>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4865513457934798007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Brad Sells" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3365948-brad-sells"><img alt="Brad Sells" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578588259p2/3365948.jpg" /></a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer171013051" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer18419360338646626562">Minutes after I finished SHADES OF EARTH:<br/><br/><b> OH. MY. STARS. I CAN'T EVEN. I SERIOUSLY <i> CAN'T EVEN. </i></b> <br/><br/>SHADES OF EARTH is seriously one of the <b> <i> <u> best </u></i></b>   finales to a YA trilogy EVER. So much action, so many secrets, so many betrayals, SO MUCH EMOTIONS. I still can't get over how much I adore this book -- and this series.<br/><br/>Guys, you are going to <b> LOVE </b> SHADES OF EARTH. It's definitely my favorite in this trilogy (and I love all of them), and Beth Revis just made this awesome and epic and wonderful and i</span>
  <span id="freeText18419360338646626562" style="display:none">Minutes after I finished SHADES OF EARTH:<br /><br /><b> OH. MY. STARS. I CAN'T EVEN. I SERIOUSLY <i> CAN'T EVEN. </i></b> <br /><br />SHADES OF EARTH is seriously one of the <b> <i> <u> best </u></i></b>   finales to a YA trilogy EVER. So much action, so many secrets, so many betrayals, SO MUCH EMOTIONS. I still can't get over how much I adore this book -- and this series.<br /><br />Guys, you are going to <b> LOVE </b> SHADES OF EARTH. It's definitely my favorite in this trilogy (and I love all of them), and Beth Revis just made this awesome and epic and wonderful and incredible book that made me feel <b> <i> ALL </i></b>  of the feels. Seriously, this book is fantastic.<br /><br />AND THAT ENDING. OH MY LORD, I THINK BETH REVIS WAS TRYING TO KILL ALL OF US. But still, that ending, and this book in general, is just amazing.<br /><br />Full review to come after I'm done fanboying. And who knows how long that will take.<br /><br /><b> My actual review: </b><br /><br />WOW. One word: WOW. Beth Revis never disappoints with her novels, and SHADES OF EARTH was one of the best conclusions to a series I have read. Props to Beth for making such an amazing, wonderful and epic trilogy! I'm going to miss these characters.<br /><br />First off, I should say that SHADES OF EARTH begins with a bang; the action begs right away and never stops. Crash landing is all that comes about Amy and Elder's mission that they have worked towards, and I think the synopsis puts it best: Almost home. But do you remember Orion? The crazy dude from the first book? All I will say is that he may have not been so crazy after all...<br /><br />Beth Revis's writing style is just incredible, with all of her novels. Right away, I was hooked and sucked back into the story along with these characters that I dearly love. I felt like I was walking around, exploring this unfamiliar and new world with these characters, and I love it that Beth Revis managed to make me feel that way in each of her books.<br /><br />Speaking of new world, can I just say that the world-building in this book was excellent? The atmosphere and all of the creatures in SHADES OF EARTH terrified me, as well as intrigued me. Gosh, why can't Hollywood finally jump on the AtU trilogy so I can see this world for myself? The author did a wonderful and fantastic job at creating and explaining the world to the reader, and all of the secrets and betrayals that occurred in this new world was brilliant.<br /><br />Also, there are SO many secrets that are revealed in SHADES OF EARTH. It is insane, yet epic at the same time. Everything that we learned that was being kept a secret from us is brought to light in this book, and when you find out what they are, your jaw will fall open.<br /><br />And that ending? HA HA HA HA WHAT WAS THAT?! I think Beth Revis was trying to kill us ALL with that ending. I will definitely not spoil it for you, but guys, there are so many turns and surprises in SHADES OF EARTH and you will not see this ending coming.<br /><br />Overall, SHADES OF EARTH is one of the best finales I have ever read about -- it's also my favorite in this trilogy. Beth Revis, thank you for making this great series. I'm so sad to see it go.</span>

<div id="review_417738701" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/417738701" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/417738701?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer417738701" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9865814493350945693"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>3 1/2 stars<br/><br/>I was so prepared to give this series conclusion four stars right up until that cheesy ending. I knew it was going to happen, I was hoping it wouldn't but, deep down, I just knew it would. I've given the first two books - <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8235178.Across_the_Universe__Across_the_Universe___1_' title='Across the Universe (Across the Universe, #1) by Beth Revis' rel='nofollow noopener'>Across the Universe</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10345927.A_Million_Suns__Across_the_Universe___2_' title='A Million Suns (Across the Universe, #2) by Beth Revis' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Million Suns</a> - four and three stars respectively, the latter rating being mainly because I thought the characters lacked development and personality, despite the fact that I love the idea behind the story. On that front, I think Ms Revis</span>
  <span id="freeText9865814493350945693" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>3 1/2 stars<br><br>I was so prepared to give this series conclusion four stars right up until that cheesy ending. I knew it was going to happen, I was hoping it wouldn't but, deep down, I just knew it would. I've given the first two books - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8235178.Across_the_Universe__Across_the_Universe___1_" title="Across the Universe (Across the Universe, #1) by Beth Revis" rel="nofollow noopener">Across the Universe</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10345927.A_Million_Suns__Across_the_Universe___2_" title="A Million Suns (Across the Universe, #2) by Beth Revis" rel="nofollow noopener">A Million Suns</a> - four and three stars respectively, the latter rating being mainly because I thought the characters lacked development and personality, despite the fact that I love the idea behind the story. On that front, I think Ms Revis finally delivered the character development I've been wanting from the start in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10345937.Shades_of_Earth__Across_the_Universe___3_" title="Shades of Earth (Across the Universe, #3) by Beth Revis" rel="nofollow noopener">Shades of Earth</a> and she served it up alongside fast-paced action, well-placed twists and a nice dose of gore. <br><br>Revis isn't afraid to give her characters a hard time, none of them make it to the end of this series unscathed and I like the way this book showcases how far they've come and how different they are now from when we were first introduced to them. Also, though it was necessary for the author to bring the romantic subplot to a head here, I admire her ability to keep it firmly in the background and not let it overtake the main issues which are survival and solving the mysteries of <i>Godspeed</i>, Orion and the new planet. Which brings me nicely to the plot of this final installment.<br><br>Elder, Amy and the members of <i>Godspeed</i> who decided to join them on the shuttle finally arrive on the new planet but - surprise! - everything doesn't go according to plan and the planet is found to be hiding numerous dark secrets and deadly creatures. The whole mystery gets even bigger with this volume before it is finally solved, Amy and Elder find themselves questioning the loyalty of those around them and the real reason why the past leader of <i>Godspeed</i> wanted to keep them from landing on this new planet. What is Centauri-Earth hiding? What has happened in the centuries that <i>Godspeed</i> has been hovering in space? And most importantly: who are the real monsters?<br><br>This series really is a kind of nerd wish-fulfillment for me. Obviously, not everyone is going to feel the same way as I do and your enjoyment of the story will depend on how much this idea appeals to you. But I love it. I don't fear technology and development... it fascinates me. Not much brings me more excitement than the possibility of discovering other planets and other lifeforms in the future. It is scary, of course it is, going into such uncharted waters as is the far corners of space, but I find it equally thrilling. There are only two places that are still so steeped in mystery that I devour stories about them with wild excitement: space and the human brain. And this series has the first completely covered.<br><br>Even though my rating has been hovering somewhere around the middle of the scale on these books, I think I can finally say that I am ready to give this series a thumbs up. If you like young adult books that are big on the mystery and action with less focus on romancing, you should love this series. Even with that cheesefest ending.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9865814493350945693" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_280790957" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/280790957" />
    <a title="Jon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4277731-jon"><img alt="Jon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384212540p2/4277731.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/280790957?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jon" href="/user/show/4277731-jon">Jon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4277731-jon?shelf=dystopia-post-apocalyptic">dystopia-post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4277731-jon?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4277731-jon?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4277731-jon?shelf=aliens">aliens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer280790957" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15551779968666282274"><a href='http://scottreadsit.blogspot.com/2013/01/shades-of-earth-by-beth-revis.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Seen at Scott Reads It</a><br/><br/><b> <i> "Space may be the final frontier but it's made in a Hollywood basement" - Red Hot Chili Peppers </i></b> <br/><br/>There will be spoilers for Across The Universe and A Million Suns. In this review there are no spoilers for Shades of Earth at all.<br/> You're probably asking yourself: "Why is he quoting the Red Hot Chili Peppers?". I have always wanted to go to space and discover new planets and stars. The likelihood of me going to space is probably is about as likely as me winning the lottery j</span>
  <span id="freeText15551779968666282274" style="display:none"><a href="http://scottreadsit.blogspot.com/2013/01/shades-of-earth-by-beth-revis.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Seen at Scott Reads It</a><br /><br /><b> <i> "Space may be the final frontier but it's made in a Hollywood basement" - Red Hot Chili Peppers </i></b> <br /><br />There will be spoilers for Across The Universe and A Million Suns. In this review there are no spoilers for Shades of Earth at all.<br /> You're probably asking yourself: "Why is he quoting the Red Hot Chili Peppers?". I have always wanted to go to space and discover new planets and stars. The likelihood of me going to space is probably is about as likely as me winning the lottery jackpot. Space has never felt so real and tangible until I read the Across The Universe trilogy. I would like to thank Revis for letting me experience the beauty and wonders of space without leaving my sofa. I was dying to read Beth Revis so on January 15th I scrambled to the library to pick up Shades Of Earth. <br /><br /> There's so much I have to say about Shades Of Earth and I don't think any review could do Shades of Earth justice. Shades of Earth leaves off right after that fantastic cliffhanger in A Million Suns. Elder and Amy have finally left Godspeed and are on Centauri-Earth trying to build a new home. The problem is that Centauri Earth is full of secrets and danger that pose a threat to our colonists.<br /><br /> Shades of Earth includes our good ol' favorites like Amy and Elder plus a whole new bunch of people from the military. We finally meet Amy's parents but the meeting isn't as pleasant as I would have hoped. Amy's Dad wants to use any means to colonize Centauri-Earth and I had an immediate distaste for him. He was so way too serious and aggressive even with his own daughter. I understand that a military leader needs to be tough and serious but he doesn't need be that way all the time. We really don't get to know Amy's mom much because Revis really focuses on Amy's Dad instead. There are so many deaths in Shades of Earth and I honestly couldn't care less about the characters who died. A majority of the characters who died in this book lacked characterization and emotional depth so when they died I wasn't affected at all. If you have tons of characters die in a book that's fine as long as affects the reader emotionally but I was rather indifferent.<br /> <br /> Even my favorite characters in the book really were frexing annoying in the beginning of the novel. Amy was acting rather childish in the beginning and she evens mentions how childish she was acting a few times. Elder wants to be tried to treated like a leader yet he doesn't act like an adult at all. Elder was constantly whining and moping how everything wasn't working out on Centauri-Earth and how he abandoned his people. I really wanted Elder to take charge and act like a true leader.<br /><br /> There is a love triangle in Shades of Earth and I wasn't a fan of the romance in this book. I really didn't find Chris appealing in anyway and from the start I had a distaste for him. Chris was an integral part of the story but feel like Revis unnecessarily made Chris a love interest. Otherwise Amy and Elder's relationship was really sweet and I really enjoyed the romance aspect of this book.<br /><br /> Shades Of Earth is a great conclusion to Revis's ATU Trilogy. I feel like everything was tied up nicely and the ending of Shades of Earth was just simply incredible. I didn't totally approve of the love triangle in this book and SoE was a little bit slower paced than the other two books. Some of the characters in this book were a bit cliche especially Amy's Dad and Chris. For the most part Shades of Earth had a very original plot with tons of plot twists that really kept me on the edge of my seat. Nevertheless despite it's flaws, I really enjoyed reading Shades of Earth! The mystery in Shades of Earth was simply captivating and engaging. I would definitely recommend reading Shades of Earth and I hope Revis writes a new book soon.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15551779968666282274" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_204097352" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/204097352" />
    <a title="Katie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3736122-katie"><img alt="Katie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524600311p2/3736122.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/204097352?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie" href="/user/show/3736122-katie">Katie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3736122-katie?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3736122-katie?shelf=penguin">penguin</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer204097352" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17975792881993351080">This has been a really great series for me. I've enjoyed watching Amy and Elder's journey since the beginning, and I think the first chapter in <i>Across the Universe</i> is one of the most well-written first chapters in YA. I've been looking forward to <i>Shades of Earth</i> since I finished <i>A Million Suns</i> in November of 2011, and I'm here to say that this book provides great closure for a great series.<br/><br/>First, I think it's important to note that this book is a lot different than the first two in that it doesn</span>
  <span id="freeText17975792881993351080" style="display:none">This has been a really great series for me. I've enjoyed watching Amy and Elder's journey since the beginning, and I think the first chapter in <i>Across the Universe</i> is one of the most well-written first chapters in YA. I've been looking forward to <i>Shades of Earth</i> since I finished <i>A Million Suns</i> in November of 2011, and I'm here to say that this book provides great closure for a great series.<br /><br />First, I think it's important to note that this book is a lot different than the first two in that it doesn't take place solely on a space ship. We're given a new world, a new setting, and this provides a lot of new options. But while I think Centauri Earth could have felt bigger, could have been this grand setting, Revis didn't necessarily take advantage of that potential. Don't get me wrong: she provided us with a lush world, but it almost felt like Amy, Elder, and the others were still confined to a small space - they really only go to three places: where the shuttle lands, their camp, and a third location I won't mention because of spoilers. They really weren't going to many more places than they did on <i>Godspeed</i>.<br /><br />For me, that gave this book (and the entire series) an almost play sort of vibe, like where there are only a few sets that actors work with. There's a sense of confinement, and while I was expecting Centauri Earth to be a breakaway from that type of setting, it was definitely not the case. I found it a little odd. Not bad, just odd.<br /><br />We're introduced to a lot of new characters in this book, namely Amy's parents. There were moments that Revis almost lost me with how she portrayed Amy's father. I think it's really easy to vilify the military - nobody likes the idea of war or weapons. And I think Revis toed the line with cliche; she didn't jump over it, as many authors do, but she got really close. But the tender moments between Amy and her father kept him real, instead of a cardboard cutout of a heartless army guy.<br /><br />But I WOULD like to rant just a tiny bit about this topic, where I don't think Revis was particularly fair (though she's certainly not the only author/person to have done this). I shall call this section "In Defense of Amy's Dad."<br /><br />*ahem*<br /><br />The entirety of <i>Shades of Earth</i> is set in a survival situation. These people are thrown into a circumstance that they know nothing about. They're being attacked by enemies they don't know. They're on a planet that's literally alien to them. And there is zero unity among the group.<br /><br />Someone HAD to take control of the situation. If not, chaos would have ensued. And no one stepped up to fill this role except for Amy's dad. Amidst the chaos, he brought order. And while Elder and Amy and a lot of other people might not have liked HOW he led, at least he DID lead.<br /><br />I was particularly annoyed with Elder in this regard, a CHILD who thought he could lead better. And yet, while he constantly complains, he never really does any actual leading. He sulks and sasses to Amy's dad, but he doesn't do much in the way of actually providing different solutions to problems. Forgive me but you, sir, are not in a place to criticize someone else's leadership when you're not willing or capable to take that person's place. If you don't like how something's being done, then you come up with something better; and don't automatically vilify someone who disagrees with you.<br /><br />/endrant<br /><br />All that being said, I didn't dislike the book. Not at all! I think the mystery is the most complex in this book than the first three, and the writing is really nice. The romance between Amy and Elder is very sweet, and I loved that Amy finally came to her senses and realized what a good guy Elder is. And I liked watching Amy mature and make responsible choices; she came a long way throughout the series, and I think her character arc was really strong.<br /><br />I also found the ending satisfying. It didn't turn out exactly the way I would have liked it to, but I think it was still good. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I do wish Elder had died, however. He would have made such a good tragic figure! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Long story short: I think fans of the series will be happy with this conclusion. I look forward to reading more by Beth Revis, and I'm happy that she wrote a straightforward science fiction novel for teens. There are spaceships, aliens, and new planets. All three of those things are ones I'd like to see more of in YA!<br /><br />...but <i>A Million Suns</i> is still my favorite.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17975792881993351080" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1917428824" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1917428824" />
    <a title="Trina (Between Chapters)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9323164-trina-between-chapters"><img alt="Trina (Between Chapters)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530495507p2/9323164.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1917428824?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trina (Between Chapters)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trina (Between Chapters)" href="/user/show/9323164-trina-between-chapters">Trina (Between Chapters)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=futuristic">futuristic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1917428824" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8765706129141433007">3 or 3.5 stars?<br/><br/>This was the most interesting installment of the trilogy to me and there were many moments that made me go 'WHOA' because of how it explored the sci-fi elements. However, some things were really predictable to me and a couple of things didn't feel fully explained in the end.<br/><br/>It's a series that got better as it went along to me, but I would have a hard time giving a blanket recommendation for it. I needed some time to sit with the type of society that was being set up but I can see </span>
  <span id="freeText8765706129141433007" style="display:none">3 or 3.5 stars?<br /><br />This was the most interesting installment of the trilogy to me and there were many moments that made me go 'WHOA' because of how it explored the sci-fi elements. However, some things were really predictable to me and a couple of things didn't feel fully explained in the end.<br /><br />It's a series that got better as it went along to me, but I would have a hard time giving a blanket recommendation for it. I needed some time to sit with the type of society that was being set up but I can see many people being turned off from the beginning.<br /><br />Overall, the thing that bothered me the most ended up being the relationship. Throughout the series the male love interest is frequently jealous of Amy talking to any other guys and his inner romantic thoughts about her ALWAYS include the word 'crushing' (he wants to crush her body to his, crush his lips against hers, crush her up against a wall) and this felt too aggressive to me. Many other elements to the story that I was uncomfortable with fell away as the series progressed, but not this. I did think the feeling of jealousy was realistic for some teenage experiences, but as an adult this wasn't a relationship I considered to be romantic at all. The romance is pretty central in this series, so whether or not you like it will probably impact how much you enjoy the books.<br /><br />I am glad I read this though because I've been curious about the series for so long and I've never read anything by Beth Revis, despite having met her twice. I would read more by her in the future, but as far as this series, there are other YA sci-fi books I'd recommend over it in a heartbeat, such as the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23395680.Illuminae__The_Illuminae_Files___1_" title="Illuminae (The Illuminae Files, #1) by Amie Kaufman" rel="nofollow noopener">Illuminae</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13138635.These_Broken_Stars__Starbound___1_" title="These Broken Stars (Starbound, #1) by Amie Kaufman" rel="nofollow noopener">These Broken Stars</a> series. I would recommend Across the Universe to readers who want a version of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6186357.The_Maze_Runner__Maze_Runner___1_" title="The Maze Runner (Maze Runner, #1) by James Dashner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Maze Runner</a> set in space, but with a more solid conclusion. For some reason, I kept getting Maze Runner vibes from this story. The characters are also trapped in one location for most of the series, are trying to figure out the truth behind their dystopian society, and also have made up curse words (though they aren't used as heavily as in TMR).</span>
  <a data-text-id="8765706129141433007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_350562176" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/350562176" />
    <a title="Braiden" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4317431-braiden"><img alt="Braiden" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456556505p2/4317431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/350562176?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Braiden" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Braiden" href="/user/show/4317431-braiden">Braiden</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4317431-braiden?shelf=ya-spec-read-and-love">ya-spec-read-and-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer350562176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2098939786694167006">WHY DID I PUT Shades of Earth OFF FOR FIFTEEN DAYS?!!! ARGHHH! Yes. Fifteen days is a long time to put off a book that was number five on your ten most anticipated books of the year. And a book that. Was. Just. Soooooooo. Good. And evil! And Good! No… IT WAS AWESOME!<br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>‘What is in our hearts is real whether we name it or let it exist only in darkness or silence.’</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>Okay. So. Beth Revis is <i>evil</i> … <i>a genius</i> … an evil genius. Why can’t all YA authors be like her? Seriously. All those other authors nee</span>
  <span id="freeText2098939786694167006" style="display:none">WHY DID I PUT Shades of Earth OFF FOR FIFTEEN DAYS?!!! ARGHHH! Yes. Fifteen days is a long time to put off a book that was number five on your ten most anticipated books of the year. And a book that. Was. Just. Soooooooo. Good. And evil! And Good! No… IT WAS AWESOME!<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>‘What is in our hearts is real whether we name it or let it exist only in darkness or silence.’</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Okay. So. Beth Revis is <i>evil</i> … <i>a genius</i> … an evil genius. Why can’t all YA authors be like her? Seriously. All those other authors need to step up to the plate and show some true bravery and release their inner mad[wo]man. It’s the words written by the psychopath side of you that will surprise whoever reads your book. It’s true. That’s something that will make me buy and read a book immediately. Speculating about what might happen would just be a huge waste of time and preparing yourself is the best that you can do – I knew since Across the Universe that Beth Revis’s books are just those you have to prepare for. But in Shades of Earth, I didn’t even think to prepare myself – there was no time to. Revis – literally – blew my mind before I had time to prepare my fortifications and protect what little innocence I had left. Her fiery barrages of surprises, twists and turns, smouldered that innocence to ash.<br /><br />Across the Universe introduced us to Godspeed, to its functioning and purpose, to Amy and Elder, and to a mysterious and thrilling new story in space. A Million Suns raised the stakes aboard Godspeed higher, tearing the civilians in two, while more revelations about Godspeed came to light. Shades of Earth raises the stakes even higher, as high as they can possibly go, as high as the tallest building in the world. Yeah, that’s high. In Shades of Earth we see the shuttle with Amy and Elder, the thousand-and-something other Godspeedians, and the eighty-or-so cryogenically frozen people land on Centauri-Earth despite a few malfunctions. Once they land a number of events occur… And that’s where I’ll stop… Shades of Earth is no happily ever after.<br /><br />What I would’ve liked to have seen is much more of Centauri Earth and the creatures that inhabit it. There certainly was quite a few twists in what little we did see of it, but just more of it would’ve been nice. Despite that, the world building is pretty incredible. Amy and Elder, the shipboards and the Earthborns, had no idea what they were getting into, had no idea what Centauri Earth is like. So Shades of Earth was quite an absorbing book as we discovered this new planet – or like I said, this corner of it – at the same time the characters did. Revis instills fear in the reader just as she instills fear in her characters, experiencing things together at the same time.<br /><br />So much has happened to these characters we’ve grown to love or despise since Across the Universe to the end of Shades of Earth. I feel like there’s much more that can happen in this universe, on this planet, with how the trilogy concluded. Beth Revis could write another trilogy or other books, further expanding, further developing, further exploring the entirety of Centauri-Earth. I have already in my dreams thought about story lines that could be written post-Shades of Earth, story lines that a season 4, a season 5, a season 6 could possibly use if these books were ever adapted for the TV. I’d even alter the very ending of Shades of Earth so that the story would further develop and continually roll out the surprises that Beth Revis is known for. If I’m given the opportunity to adapt these books to the TV I would do it with dignity, with respect, with a love for the source material. But I digress.<br /><br />The plot in Shades of Earth continually evolved, continually kept you questioning, on your feet, running, hiding, gasping for air, in astonishment, in terror, in shock. BOOM! BOOM! BOOM! this book went, the explosions galore helping me since I did not have to shave before work the next day. The trilogy arc is something I’ve been quite impressed with – one of the best I’ve ever had the pleasure of reading. Whoever at Razorbill/Penguin told Beth Revis that the story could develop after Across the Universe, whoever pushed Beth Revis to write another two books, whoever believed in Beth Revis and her divine storytelling and the potential in life after Across the Universe should be awarded a medal of some kind. Seriously. Revis had a plan since the start and it ended in ways I did not expect. Shades of Earth was an explosive conclusion, raining down revelations and debris all around.<br /><br />I must add something that I took notice of and must spotlight. There was this new character Adam. He was made to be a new love interest for Amy, someone to cause tension and conflict between Amy and Elder. But to be honest, whoever calls that a love triangle is seriously mistaken. Yes, she was attracted to his looks. Yes, she flirted. Yes, they spent some time together. But there was a moment where Adam leaned in towards Amy to give her a kiss. But Amy refused it, turning her head away. I had always loved Amy since the beginning, but this moment proved that she was mature, not constantly seeking attention, not wanting to make out and be with every guy she finds attractive under the sun. Because she is with Elder. And Elder is with her. This shows that she’s head-strong. This shows that she’s loyal – to Elder, as well as to others. It was a trait of hers that I found to be the most memorable. I guess I have to talk about Elder now too? Well, Elder was great. He was loyal, driven, brave, and determined to protect Amy and everyone, even those he had rivalled with in the past, putting himself in harm’s way for the betterment of everybody else. He was a hero; she was a heroine. Together they were gold.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>‘I learned that life is so, so fragile. I learned that you can know someone for just days and never forget the impression he left on you. I learned that art can be beautiful and sad at the same time. I learned that if someone loves you, he’ll wait for you to love him back. I learned that how much you want something doesn’t determine whether you get it or not, that “no” might not be enough, that life isn’t fair, that my parents can’t save me, that maybe no one can.’</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />The conclusion to this trilogy is one not be missed. Although it might leave you with post traumatic stress disorder for the rest of your life, Shades of Earth is worth it. Whatever other book Beth Revis comes out with will be worth it. Being Beth Revis right at this moment would be a pretty good feeling. If I ever meet Beth… When I meet Beth… oh, man, I cannot fathom not meeting Beth and not being able to stroke the head that holds that brain built from epicness, the brain that produced such an awesome trilogy that is the Across the Universe trilogy.<br /><br />Hi, Beth! … … … … *flails*<br /><br /><br />--------<br /><br /><s>fuckfuckfuckityfuckfuck.... i hate the new covers; I DESPISE THEM! Hopefully UK covers continue the same way they were going so at least my original hardcovers can match in SOME way.<br /><br />Edit: THANK YOU to the UK publisher for creating a cover along the same lines as the original two, and although it's a bit different it's at least much closer to the originals than the US redesigned.</s><br /><br />*I've been seeing pictures of the physical copy of the hardcover and I must say it's not as bad as the so called powers of the internet perceive it to be like. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2098939786694167006" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Kat (Lost in Neverland)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland"><img alt="Kat (Lost in Neverland)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417030210p2/5749698.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/331606259?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat (Lost in Neverland)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat (Lost in Neverland)" href="/user/show/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland">Kat (Lost in Neverland)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer331606259" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8502197524963553708">Ah, I'm very excited for this book. Know why? <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1407973301i/10789985.jpg' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><br/>Aliens are coming. <i>Aliens.</i><br/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380378059ra/733489.gif' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407973301ra/10789986.gif' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/><b>Update:</b> Seriously, what the FUCK is up with that cover? That does not match the first two and probably will look like crap next to my ATU and AMS. <br/><br/></span>
  <span id="freeText8502197524963553708" style="display:none">Ah, I'm very excited for this book. Know why? <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1407973301i/10789985.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><br>Aliens are coming. <i>Aliens.</i><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380378059ra/733489.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407973301ra/10789986.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>Update:</b> Seriously, what the FUCK is up with that cover? That does not match the first two and probably will look like crap next to my ATU and AMS. <br><br></span>

<div id="review_1536950029" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1536950029" />
    <a title="Adita ✨The Slumbering Insomniac✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37265034-adita-the-slumbering-insomniac"><img alt="Adita ✨The Slumbering Insomniac✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1467396795p2/37265034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1536950029?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adita ✨The Slumbering Insomniac✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adita ✨The Slumbering Insomniac✨" href="/user/show/37265034-adita-the-slumbering-insomniac">Adita ✨The Slumbering Insomniac✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37265034-adita-the-slumbering-insomniac?shelf=couldnot-get-enough-of-it">couldnot-get-enough-of-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37265034-adita-the-slumbering-insomniac?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37265034-adita-the-slumbering-insomniac?shelf=ibooks">ibooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37265034-adita-the-slumbering-insomniac?shelf=late-winter-chill">late-winter-chill</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37265034-adita-the-slumbering-insomniac?shelf=adorable-thats-what-i-thought">adorable-thats-what-i-thought</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37265034-adita-the-slumbering-insomniac?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37265034-adita-the-slumbering-insomniac?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37265034-adita-the-slumbering-insomniac?shelf=i-heart-it">i-heart-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37265034-adita-the-slumbering-insomniac?shelf=isthisall-i-want-a-sequel">isthisall-i-want-a-sequel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37265034-adita-the-slumbering-insomniac?shelf=one-million-fireflies">one-million-fireflies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1536950029" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer232486846171197143">(This is an all-inclusive review for the trilogy.) <br/><br/>★★★★★★★★★★[10/10]<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457703974i/18391345.jpg' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13335037.Divergent__Divergent___1_' title='Divergent (Divergent, #1) by Veronica Roth' rel='nofollow noopener'>Divergent</a>. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games___1_' title='The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) by Suzanne Collins' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Hunger Games</a>. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11106458.The_Mortal_Instruments__The_Mortal_Instruments__1_4_' title='The Mortal Instruments (The Mortal Instruments #1-4) by Cassandra Clare' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Mortal Instruments</a>. I can't believe that they made movies out of those, instead of <b>this</b>. If they deemed twelve crazy districts and five pointless factions fit to be shown on screens, then they should have guessed that people would love to see <b>Godspeed</b> making its way across the universe too. The movie <b>"Passengers"</b> might be a consolation, but I assure you, Amy Martin and Elder Davis's adventure is </span>
  <span id="freeText232486846171197143" style="display:none">(This is an all-inclusive review for the trilogy.) <br><br>★★★★★★★★★★[10/10]<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457703974i/18391345.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13335037.Divergent__Divergent___1_" title="Divergent (Divergent, #1) by Veronica Roth" rel="nofollow noopener">Divergent</a>. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games___1_" title="The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hunger Games</a>. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11106458.The_Mortal_Instruments__The_Mortal_Instruments__1_4_" title="The Mortal Instruments (The Mortal Instruments #1-4) by Cassandra Clare" rel="nofollow noopener">The Mortal Instruments</a>. I can't believe that they made movies out of those, instead of <b>this</b>. If they deemed twelve crazy districts and five pointless factions fit to be shown on screens, then they should have guessed that people would love to see <b>Godspeed</b> making its way across the universe too. The movie <b>"Passengers"</b> might be a consolation, but I assure you, Amy Martin and Elder Davis's adventure is far more thrilling than that of Aurora Dunn and Jim Preston's. <br><br>Trilogies are always a fly in the ointment for readers. It takes all of your patience and that of the entire population of the world to get to the end of the third book (doesn't mean quadrilogies are any better; and I don't even want to think about Mortal Instruments). But, this one rekindled my faith in trilogies all over again. The world of Elder and Amy that Beth Revis painted is as beautiful as that of Harley's Koi Fish. Right from the spaceship Godspeed to the relief and topography of <b>Centauri-Earth</b> and the scientific details of shuttle launch and ship manoeuvring and high-octane landing, she has built the world to spectacular precision. What's better -- the story gets better as it progresses, with a lot of unexpected twists and savoury turns along the way.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483875751i/21657548.png" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>▶<u>
  <b>STRENGTHS:<br><br>CHARACTERS:</b>
</u><br><br>There is Amy. She is supposed to be dead many centuries ago, but science has made it possible for her to wake up from her cold sleep like she has just had a catnap. She is smart, thrusty and doesn't believe in "love at first sight". She fights to establish her identity in a place where she finds herself to be a loner. Though she is not our typical kickass belle, she can very easily be one with a bit of touch-up. <br><br>And then there is <b>
  <i>
    <u>Elder</u>
  </i>
</b>. Describing Elder does the job of describing his mentor Eldest and his supposed-to-be mentor Orion too, but Elder isn't in any way either of them, although they are the same - technically<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(ooh..clones!!) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483875751i/21657549.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>You can count the rest of the memorable characters with one hand, but that won't help you to zero in on the potential bad guys in all of the three books. Beth Revis adeptly picks out all the important characters - Kit, Maria Martin, Colonel Martin, Emma Bledsoe, Doc, Dr. Gupta, Harvey - one by one, that at the end of the book, none of the characters that grew on you actually survives -- but, you can never hate her for George Martinesque decisions. <br><br><b>STORY LINE:</b><br><br>At the end of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8235178.Across_the_Universe__Across_the_Universe___1_" title="Across the Universe (Across the Universe, #1) by Beth Revis" rel="nofollow noopener">Across the Universe</a>, you get an answer to why Amy was woken up decades before she was due. At the end of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10345927.A_Million_Suns__Across_the_Universe___2_" title="A Million Suns (Across the Universe, #2) by Beth Revis" rel="nofollow noopener">A Million Suns</a>, you get an answer to why Centauri-Earth is forever out of reach of the Sol-Earthlings. At the end of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10345937.Shades_of_Earth__Across_the_Universe___3_" title="Shades of Earth (Across the Universe, #3) by Beth Revis" rel="nofollow noopener">Shades of Earth</a>, you are ready to believe that man will always be man's mortal enemy wherever he goes, and will get the much needed answer to why the entire mission was botched up in the first place. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483875751i/21657550.jpg" width="300" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But, that's just it -- <i>you have to wait till the end of every book to know what you are supposed to know</i>; Beth Revis made sure that you'll <i>fail at your guessing game</i> every single time. <br><br>And this is the first time I found myself focussing more on the crux of the story rather than waiting for the sporadic romance - it came unexpected, leaving the original flow of the story unhindered, like an appendage that you could remove at your will - whereas in most of the YA series I have read so far, I usually start counting the kisses when I am almost halfway through the third installment -- just to suppress a yawn. <br><br>The end was a bit of a cliché, but sometimes, isn't it cliché that we are all looking for? <br>And, kudos to the author, this is the first time that fiction had me convinced that we are not alone in the universe, and that women can write super-duper, space-trooper novels, that.. well, make a lot of sense. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483875751i/21657551._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(The ship - what did I say about Beth Revis being a skilled shuttle designer?)<br><br>▶ <b>WEAKNESSES: </b><br>I'll tell you if I can think of any. Or, why don't you see it for yourself?</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="232486846171197143" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer362592748" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer959674619648168560"><b>Initial Reaction:</b> Damn. I love the title. Can't wait to see the cover!<br/><br/><b>Final Reaction:</b> That cover is a joke...<i>right?</i> </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_333188439" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/333188439" />
    <a title="Kristalia " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5705623-kristalia"><img alt="Kristalia " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535637983p2/5705623.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/333188439?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristalia " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristalia " href="/user/show/5705623-kristalia">Kristalia </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=favorite-couple">favorite-couple</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=unique-or-different-story">unique-or-different-story</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=type-book-extras">type-book-extras</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer333188439" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15587706754435858334"><b>Final rating: 5/5 stars</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"But there’s a difference, isn’t there? Between saying goodbye and death."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><b> One word: omfgthiswassofrexingepicthatihavenowordslefttoexpresswhatithink...</b><br/>there, i wrote it XD<br/><br/>Anyway. <b>Awesome conclusion </b> to one of my favorite ya sci fi series. I am glad that Beth Revis didn't fail me with all her glorious plot twists and awesomeness. I liked every moment of it, and i just can't help but think that i would love if this book was longer! It seemed to me too short, but </span>
  <span id="freeText15587706754435858334" style="display:none"><b>Final rating: 5/5 stars</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"But there’s a difference, isn’t there? Between saying goodbye and death."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b> One word: omfgthiswassofrexingepicthatihavenowordslefttoexpresswhatithink...</b><br />there, i wrote it XD<br /><br />Anyway. <b>Awesome conclusion </b> to one of my favorite ya sci fi series. I am glad that Beth Revis didn't fail me with all her glorious plot twists and awesomeness. I liked every moment of it, and i just can't help but think that i would love if this book was longer! It seemed to me too short, but still, there wasn't anything that was missing or anything out of place.<br /><br />____________________________________________<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <u>Story</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br />____________________________________________<br /><br />Story was awesome as always. Beth Revis was quite sadistic to torture people with her chapter endings...especially near the end, concerning one person (i almost had heart attack!). <br /><br />Anyway, everything was properly connected, there weren't any plot holes, and what i liked the most was that she developed Amy and Elder's characters even more! Even threw in new ones like Chris (which i majestically laugh now because we share the Chris part of the name), Amy's parents and all of the frozens. Throw in some aliens, weird planet and deaths every day and you have perfect entertainment. <br /><br />Oh and btw, i adored it that the book wasn't all about the romance between the two of them (you can say though that there was mini love triangle).<br /><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>" “We all die someday." Maybe the only thing that makes that fact bearable is the idea that death is the only way we can return to the stars.” "<br /></b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />____________________________________________<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <u>Characters</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br />____________________________________________<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <u> Elder </u>
  </i>
</b>: i just love him so freaking much. Anyway, once all that happened was his responsibility, he always had to take care of everything and everyone, and his hardest decision was to leave the people on Godspeed. After the awakening of the frozens, he becomes just one of the <i>those</i> shipborns, and he had hard time to prove to Earthlings that he was the one who was leader of his people. So...the way they treated him and kept him in the shadows just awoke his doubt of Sol-Earthians motives. He starts believing in what Orion had said. He thought about everything, and always went forward with his decisions, and some of them were pretty much reckless. Still, he is adorable and fluffy as always.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <u> Amy </u>
  </i>
</b>: Sometimes i just wanted to smack her in the face and say "what is wrong with you??? Girl, you need to work on screaming at parents to listen to you carefully before they screw up everything!!!", or Elder should have done it....But damn....Still, i hate it that even though she was first Earth human to awake, no one even bothered to listen to her until everything was late. Still, there is no question that she is brave as well, but she seemed more naive here than in the other books. In the end she was awesome....The end.<br /> <br /><b>
  <i>
    <u> Chris </u>
  </i>
</b>: asdjasldjasjkdjlasjd i didn't like you but now i do! <br /> <blockquote><br /><b>Me</b>: I don't trust you. You are to shady.<br /><b>Chris</b>: I am not asking you to. But...<br /><b>Me</b>: No but, i saw what you did there!<br /><b>Chris</b>: But, but...i...if you would just listen...<br /><b>Me</b>: i am the reader, i see everything, i know everything and damn you kept some nasty stuff cutie pie.<br /><b>Chris</b>: ...<br /><b>Me</b>: But i still like you :D Though i must say that i didn't expect it. At all. </blockquote><br />Ok, i have lost my mind....<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <u> Amy's parents and other people: </u>
  </i>
</b>: Amy's dad is an asshole. At least that is what i thought till the end. And i still think it. Actually, everyone from Earth turned out to be more assholier than any other asshole in the previous books. Except Emma and Amy's mom. One thing i must say about <b>
  <i>
    <u> Orion: </u>
  </i>
</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ he was after all, right to the bone, and i am sad that he had to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ die that way, and die blind without even seeing anything in the end  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I felt sorry for him even in the first book, and i don't think that he deserved what happened. If only Elder had listened....  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Oh, i almost forgot! Amy and Elder had <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ seeeeeex xDDD  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>!!!<br /><br />____________________________________________<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <u>Overall</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br />____________________________________________<br /><br />GO.READ.THE WHOLE SERIES NOW IF YOU HAVEN'T!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!<br />i need to read it again...i need more of Elder!!! Now!!!!!!!<br />____________________________________________<br /><br />● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ●<br />____________________________________________ <br /><br /><b>REVIEW(S) RELATED TO THIS BOOK:</b><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/333188423" rel="nofollow noopener">Across the Universe (Across the Universe, #1) </a> <br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/333188426" rel="nofollow noopener"> A Million Suns (Across the Universe #2) </a> <br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/333188439" rel="nofollow noopener"> Shades of Earth (Across the Universe, #3) </a> <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10955682849883740271">* 4.5/5 stars.<br/>Wow, that was so good! What a great way to end this trilogy. I loved the first book, Across the Universe, was a bit underwhelmed by the second book, A Million Suns, and then got pleasantly surprised by this one! The best part of the book was definitely the plot. Beth Revis had the tough task of introducing a whole new planet into the story while also wrapping up plot lines from the previous books, and she managed to do that oh, so well. The story took so many twists and turns and I</span>
  <span id="freeText10955682849883740271" style="display:none">* 4.5/5 stars.<br />Wow, that was so good! What a great way to end this trilogy. I loved the first book, Across the Universe, was a bit underwhelmed by the second book, A Million Suns, and then got pleasantly surprised by this one! The best part of the book was definitely the plot. Beth Revis had the tough task of introducing a whole new planet into the story while also wrapping up plot lines from the previous books, and she managed to do that oh, so well. The story took so many twists and turns and I loved every one of them!</span>
